    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">قَرُبَ</orth>
                  </form>, i. e., like <foreign lang="ar">تَعِبَ</foreign> and like <foreign lang="ar">قَتَلَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قِرْبَانٌ</foreign>, signifies <hi rend="ital">I did the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affair;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, near,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I approached, to it,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to doing it</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">to doing something with it</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to it</hi>]: an ex. of the former meaning is the saying [in the Kur xvii. 34], <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَقْرَبُوا ٱلزِّنَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Commit not ye fornication,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">adultery;</hi> or, accord. to some, this is an ex. of the latter meaning]; and hence one says, <foreign lang="ar">قَرِبْتُ المَرْأَةَ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">قِرْبَانٌ</foreign>, a metonymical phrase, meaning <hi rend="ital">I compressed the woman:</hi> and an ex. of the latter meaning is the saying, <foreign lang="ar">لَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">تَقْرَبُوا الحِمَى</foreign> i. e. <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَدْنُوا مِنْهُ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">Approach not ye to doing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to entering upon, the thing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">place, that is prohibited,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">interdicted</hi>]. (Msb.) And the Arabs say, of a man, when a thing has disquieted, or disturbed, and grieved, him, <foreign lang="ar">أَخَذَهُ مَا قَرُبَ وَمَا بَعُدَ</foreign>, as though meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He became,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">has become, disquieted by reason of near and remote circumstances of his case:</hi> (O:) or <hi rend="ital">recent and old griefs took hold upon him.</hi> (Mgh in art. <foreign lang="ar">قدم</foreign>. [See art. <foreign lang="ar">بعد</foreign>.]) <foreign lang="ar">دَنَا مِنِّى وَقَرُبَ</foreign> is expl. by Zj as meaning <hi rend="ital">He drew near to me and drew nearer.</hi> (T in art. <foreign lang="ar">دلو</foreign>: see 5 in that art.) [And several other verbs belonging to this art. are syn., or nearly so, with <foreign lang="ar">قَرُبَ</foreign> or with <foreign lang="ar">قَرِبَ</foreign> in senses expl. above. Thus   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35387-1" target="اقرب" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> is <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi>

(TA.)   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n35387-2" target="اقترب" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, also, is <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَرُبَ</foreign> in the first of the senses expl. above; (MA;) [i. e.] it is <hi rend="ital">syn. with</hi>

                  <hi rend="ital">A kind of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سِقَآء</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">skin</hi>], (S, * O, * TA,) <hi rend="ital">used for water:</hi> (S, O:) or <hi rend="ital">a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَطْب</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">skin</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that is used for milk,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">sometimes for water:</hi> (ISd, K:) or <hi rend="ital">such as is sewed on one side:</hi> (K:) [the modern <foreign lang="ar">قِرْبَة</foreign>, which is seldom, if ever, used for anything but water, is (if I may judge from my own observations and the accounts of others) always made of the skin of a goat about one year old or upwards: it consists of nearly the whole skin; only the skin of the head, and a small portion of that of each leg, being cut off: it has a seam extending from the upper part of the throat nearly to the belly, and sometimes a corresponding seam at the hinder part, but more commonly only a patch of leather over the fundament and navel: over the seam, or over each seam, is sewed a narrow strip of leather; and a mouth of leather is added in the place of the head: it is carried on the back, by means of a strap, or cord, &amp;c., one end of which is generally attached to a cord connecting the two fore-legs; and the other, to the right hind leg:] the pl.
